      <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens_(soundtrack)" title="Star Wars: The Force Awakens (soundtrack)">Star Wars: The Force Awakens (soundtrack)</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:25%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;"> 
      <div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;"> 
       <div> 
        <p>It's all a continuation of an initial set of ideas. It's a bit like adding paragraphs to a letter that's been going on for a number of years. Starting with a completely new film, a story that I don't know, characters that I haven't met, my whole approach to writing music is completely different—trying to find an identity, trying to find melodic identifications if that's needed for the characters, and so on.</p> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <cite style="display: block; text-align: right;">—John Williams on returning to the <i>Star Wars</i> universe<sup id="cite_ref-Williams_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Williams-181">[181]</a></sup></cite>
     </div> 
     <p>In July 2013, <a href="/wiki/John_Williams" title="John Williams">John Williams</a> was confirmed to compose the score.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> The music for the film's first two trailers was reworked from earlier Williams compositions.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AFM_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFM-185">[185]</a></sup> He began working on the film in December 2014, and by June 2015 had been through most of the film reels, working on a daily basis.<sup id="cite_ref-AFM_185-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFM-185">[185]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-variety.com_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-variety.com-186">[186]</a></sup> In May 2015, Williams stated that he would return to themes from the previous films, such as ones for Luke, Leia and Han, in ways that "will seem very natural and right in the moments for which we've chosen to do these kinds of quotes. There aren't many of them, but there are a few that I think are important and will seem very much a part of the fabric of the piece in a positive and constructive way." He said that working with Abrams was similar to the process he went through with Lucas in the earlier films.<sup id="cite_ref-Williams_181-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Williams-181">[181]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Recording sessions for <i>The Force Awakens</i> began in June 2015 at the <a href="/wiki/Sony_Pictures_Studios" title="Sony Pictures Studios">Sony Pictures Studios</a>' Barbra Streisand Scoring Stage in Culver City, with <a href="/wiki/William_Ross_(composer)" title="William Ross (composer)">William Ross</a> conducting most of the music.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> The first day of recording was June 1, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> Williams attended the sessions and conducted the remainder of the recordings.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Williams said the recording process was "very luxurious", with 12 sessions scattered over a five-month period between June and November. The score was recorded by a freelance orchestra, with sessions continuing on and off over that five-month period. The 90-piece orchestra recorded 175 minutes of music, although nearly an hour of that was discarded, modified, or rerecorded as Abrams re-edited the film. Williams's theme for Snoke was recorded by a 24-voice men's chorus. <a href="/wiki/Gustavo_Dudamel" title="Gustavo Dudamel">Gustavo Dudamel</a> conducted the opening and end title music for the film at Williams' behest.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> Recording of the score was completed on November 14, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-AFM_185-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFM-185">[185]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-variety.com_186-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-variety.com-186">[186]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> The film's soundtrack was released by <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Records" title="Walt Disney Records">Walt Disney Records</a> on December 18, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> Williams's score is more than two hours long.<sup id="cite_ref-variety.com_186-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-variety.com-186">[186]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Lin-Manuel_Miranda" title="Lin-Manuel Miranda">Lin-Manuel Miranda</a> and Abrams contributed music to the film's cantina scene, similar to the <a href="/wiki/Mos_Eisley_Cantina" title="Mos Eisley Cantina">Mos Eisley Cantina</a>. Abrams met Miranda at a performance of his Broadway musical <i><a href="/wiki/Hamilton_(musical)" title="Hamilton (musical)">Hamilton</a></i>, where Miranda jokingly offered to compose the cantina music, should it be needed. Unknown to Miranda, Williams had previously told Abrams that he did not want to compose the music for that scene, wanting to focus on the orchestral score for the film. Abrams then contacted Miranda, and the two began to collaborate on the music for the scene, over a period of two months.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>South Korean boy band <a href="/wiki/EXO_(band)" title="EXO (band)" class="mw-redirect">EXO</a> released their song "Lightsaber" in collaboration with the film for its release in their home country on November 11.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup> The promoted track was subsequently released as part of their <i><a href="/wiki/Sing_for_You_(EP)" title="Sing for You (EP)">Sing for You</a></i> album with a Chinese version,<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> as well as also being released in Japanese.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> Chinese pop singer <a href="/wiki/Luhan_(singer)" title="Luhan (singer)">Luhan</a> provided the Chinese theme "Inner Force" for the Chinese release of the film.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release">Release</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Release">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <p><i>Star Wars: The Force Awakens</i> premiered in Los Angeles at the <a href="/wiki/TCL_Chinese_Theatre" title="TCL Chinese Theatre">TCL Chinese Theatre</a>, <a href="/wiki/El_Capitan_Theatre" title="El Capitan Theatre">El Capitan Theatre</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dolby_Theatre" title="Dolby Theatre">Dolby Theatre</a> on December 14, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-premiere_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-premiere-199">[199]</a></sup> A white tent stretched along <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Boulevard" title="Hollywood Boulevard">Hollywood Boulevard</a> from Orange Drive to <a href="/wiki/Highland_Avenue_(Los_Angeles)" title="Highland Avenue (Los Angeles)">Highland Avenue</a>, covering the "massive" premiere event that hosted more than five thousand guests.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> The film was released in 12 countries including European nations (such as Italy and France, releasing it on a Wednesday), the Philippines and Thailand on December 16; 32 countries including the United Kingdom (releasing on a Thursday), Mexico and additional European, Asian, African, South American and Oceania countries on December 17; and in North America, Japan, Spain, and Venezuela on December 18,<sup id="cite_ref-THRReleases_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-THRReleases-201">[201]</a></sup> in 3D and IMAX 3D.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup> It was released in India on December 25<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> and in China on January 9, 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-THRReleases_201-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-THRReleases-201">[201]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>In North America, it had the widest release of December across 4,134 theaters of which 3,300 were 3D locations, a record 392 IMAX screens (13 of which are <a href="/wiki/70_mm_film" title="70 mm film">70mm</a>), 451 premium large format screens, 146 <a href="/wiki/D-Box_Technologies" title="D-Box Technologies">D-Box</a> locations,<sup id="cite_ref-theforce1_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theforce1-204">[204]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-theforce2_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theforce2-205">[205]</a></sup> as well as releasing in the <a href="/wiki/HDR10" title="HDR10" class="mw-redirect">Dolby Vision</a> format (<a href="/wiki/High-dynamic-range_rendering" title="High-dynamic-range rendering">High dynamic range</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rec._2020" title="Rec. 2020">Rec. 2020</a> color) in <a href="/wiki/Dolby_Cinema" title="Dolby Cinema">Dolby Cinema</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup> Worldwide, it will be released across 940 IMAX theaters, a new record.<sup id="cite_ref-theforce2_205-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theforce2-205">[205]</a></sup> On December 18, 2015, the film began playing on every IMAX screen in North America for four straight weeks up to January 14, 2016. This made it the first film since <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros." title="Warner Bros.">Warner Bros. Pictures</a>' <a href="/wiki/The_Hobbit_(film_series)" title="The Hobbit (film series)"><i>The Hobbit</i> trilogy</a> to receive such a release.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup> The film finally shed some of its IMAX screens with the release of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Revenant_(2015_film)" title="The Revenant (2015 film)">The Revenant</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Finest_Hours_(2016_film)" title="The Finest Hours (2016 film)">The Finest Hours</a></i> in mid-January 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>On November 6, 2014, the film's title was announced as <i>Star Wars: The Force Awakens</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-title_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-title-209">[209]</a></sup> Similarly to <i>The Empire Strikes Back</i> and <i>Return of the Jedi</i>, "Episode VII" was included in the film's <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_opening_crawl" title="Star Wars opening crawl">opening crawl</a>, but not in its official title.<sup id="cite_ref-geller_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geller-210">[210]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-crawl_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crawl-211">[211]</a></sup> In December 2015, Pablo Hidalgo, the creative executive at the Lucasfilm Story Group which handles all the canonical continuity for the <i>Star Wars</i> universe, revealed that the working title for the film was <i>Shadow of the Empire</i> "for the longest time".<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> Advance ticket sales for the film began on October 19, 2015,<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> and were in strong demand, resulting in online movie ticket sites crashing.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Vue_Cinemas" title="Vue Cinemas">Vue Cinemas</a>, the United Kingdom's third-largest theater chain, sold 45,000 tickets in 24 hours, 10,000 of which were sold in 90 minutes, a record for the theater.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup> In the United States, the film pre-sold a record-breaking $6.5 million worth of IMAX ticket sales on a single day. IMAX has never previously registered more than $1 million in pre-sales on a single day.<sup id="cite_ref-IMAXsales_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMAXsales-217">[217]</a></sup> In total it sold over $50 million in pre-sales breaking the record.<sup id="cite_ref-THG_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-THG-218">[218]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-THRproj_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-THRproj-219">[219]</a></sup> This number was raised to $100 million including $50–60 million in advance ticket sales by December 14.<sup id="cite_ref-THRproj_219-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-THRproj-219">[219]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Deadproj_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Deadproj-220">[220]</a></sup> However, not all tickets that were pre-sold were for the film's opening weekend, with <a href="/wiki/Fandango_(ticket_service)" title="Fandango (ticket service)">Fandango</a> President Paul Yanover saying "people have set aside tickets for screenings in January, weeks after the big opening... We have people buying <i>Star Wars</i> [<i>The Force Awakens</i>] into 2016. It's not just an opening-weekend phenomenon."<sup id="cite_ref-THG_218-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-THG-218">[218]</a></sup> Similarly, the film broke pre-sales records in the UK,<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup> Canada,<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup> and Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The film is the first live-action <i>Star Wars</i> film not to be released theatrically by <a href="/wiki/20th_Century_Fox" title="20th Century Fox">20th Century Fox</a>; accordingly the film is not introduced with either that company's <a href="/wiki/Fox_Fanfare" title="Fox Fanfare" class="mw-redirect">logo, or its signature fanfare</a> composed by <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Newman_(composer)" title="Alfred Newman (composer)">Alfred Newman</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup> Shortly following Disney's acquisition of Lucasfilm, the studio had indicated that the then-untitled film would be released under the "<a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Pictures">Disney</a>|Lucasfilm" branding,<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup> similar to the branding used for <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_Rebels" title="Star Wars Rebels">Star Wars Rebels</a></i>, and akin to the "Disney·Pixar" co-branding of <a href="/wiki/Pixar" title="Pixar">Pixar</a>-produced films released by <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Pictures">Walt Disney Pictures</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup> Ultimately, Disney's logo was absent from the film's marketing—but nevertheless, appeared on merchandise—and the film was released with only Lucasfilm's <a href="/wiki/Production_logo" title="Production logo">production logo</a> shown silently before the main titles;<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup> Disney chairman <a href="/wiki/Bob_Iger" title="Bob Iger">Bob Iger</a> explained the change by saying it was "for the fans".<sup id="cite_ref-screencrush-iger_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-screencrush-iger-228">[228]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing">Marketing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Marketing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>On November 28, 2014, Lucasfilm released a 90-second <a href="/wiki/Teaser_campaign" title="Teaser campaign">teaser trailer</a> to promote <i>The Force Awakens</i>. It was screened in selected cinemas across the United States and Canada and in theaters worldwide in December 2014. It was also released on <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> and the <a href="/wiki/ITunes_Store" title="ITunes Store">iTunes Store</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-TraileriTunes_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TraileriTunes-229">[229]</a></sup> generating a record 58.2 million views on YouTube in its first week.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup> Critics compared the brief footage favorably to the production values of the original trilogy. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hollywood_Reporter" title="The Hollywood Reporter">The Hollywood Reporter</a></i> called the trailer "perfectly potent nostalgia", praising its mix of old and new.<sup id="cite_ref-hollywoodreporter_281114_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hollywoodreporter_281114-231">[231]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Empire_(film_magazine)" title="Empire (film magazine)">Empire</a></i> was impressed by the continuity with the first films – "the <i>feel</i> of classic <i>Star Wars</i>" – but noted the absence of Hamill, Ford, and Fisher and speculated about the significance of the new characters.<sup id="cite_ref-empire_281114_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-empire_281114-232">[232]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> wrote that the use of the <i>Star Wars</i> fanfare by John Williams reinforced <a href="/wiki/Brand_loyalty" title="Brand loyalty">brand loyalty</a> among fans.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_011214_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian_011214-233">[233]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Star_wars_force_awakens_film_promotion_nuremberg_2015.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Star_wars_force_awakens_film_promotion_nuremberg_2015.JPG/220px-Star_wars_force_awakens_film_promotion_nuremberg_2015.JPG" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Star_wars_force_awakens_film_promotion_nuremberg_2015.JPG/330px-Star_wars_force_awakens_film_promotion_nuremberg_2015.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Star_wars_force_awakens_film_promotion_nuremberg_2015.JPG/440px-Star_wars_force_awakens_film_promotion_nuremberg_2015.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3840" data-file-height="2160"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Star_wars_force_awakens_film_promotion_nuremberg_2015.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Large-scale outdoor advertising for 
        <i>Star Wars: The Force Awakens</i> in the city centre of Nuremberg, Germany
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>On December 11, 2014, Abrams and Kennedy released a series of eight mock <a href="/wiki/Topps" title="Topps">Topps</a> <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_trading_card" title="Star Wars trading card">trading cards</a> revealing the names of several characters.<sup id="cite_ref-CharacterNames_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CharacterNames-234">[234]</a></sup> On April 16, 2015, a second teaser trailer, this one lasting two minutes, was shown at the opening panel at the <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_Celebration" title="Star Wars Celebration"><i>Star Wars</i> Celebration</a> in <a href="/wiki/Anaheim,_California" title="Anaheim, California">Anaheim, California</a>. Lucasfilm president Kathleen Kennedy said the reaction to the trailer was "staggering... the entire room of almost eight thousand people just leapt to their feet and roared, I mean I can't think of anything I've ever been to – other than a rock concert – that felt quite like that."<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup> The trailer was viewed over 88 million times within the first 24 hours of release, breaking the record.<sup id="cite_ref-Yahoo_236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo-236">[236]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Forbes_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes-237">[237]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness World Records</a>, the second teaser trailer amassed 30.65 million in 24 hours, setting a new world record for the "most viewed movie trailer on YouTube in 24 hours."<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">[238]</a></sup> The event was broadcast live by <a href="/wiki/Verizon" title="Verizon" class="mw-redirect">Verizon</a> on YouTube, StarWars.com and in movie theaters. The trailer shows many of the new characters and the first footage of Chewbacca and Han Solo. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Huffington_Post" title="The Huffington Post">The Huffington Post</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s Graham Milne wrote that the trailer "was an affirmation of something that we'd long been told was never going to happen. This was a gift. This was faith rewarded. About damn time."<sup id="cite_ref-The_Huffington_Post_239-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Huffington_Post-239">[239]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><i><a href="/wiki/Vanity_Fair_(magazine)" title="Vanity Fair (magazine)">Vanity Fair</a></i> was the first magazine to release an exclusive cover issue devoted to <i>The Force Awakens</i>. The magazine, released on May 7, 2015, featured exclusive interviews and photos of the cast photographed by <a href="/wiki/Annie_Leibovitz" title="Annie Leibovitz">Annie Leibovitz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Vanity_Fair_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vanity_Fair-240">[240]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Vanity_Fair_2_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vanity_Fair_2-241">[241]</a></sup> At the 2015 <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Comic-Con_International" title="San Diego Comic-Con International">San Diego Comic-Con International</a>, in addition to a panel with many of the actors, a behind-the-scenes look at the film demonstrated the film's use of practical sets and effects. It was positively received, with Nigel M. Smith of <i>The Guardian</i> writing: "The featurette's angle is a strong one and connects with fans of the original trilogy in an incredibly poignant way. It also does a sly job of teasing Fisher's new look as Leia and Simon Pegg's mysterious involvement as a rumored alien in the movie, without actually showing the actors in action." Smith compared the marketing strategy for the film to that of a previous Abrams film, <i><a href="/wiki/Super_8_(film)" title="Super 8 (film)">Super 8</a></i>, saying "the promos... are notable for what they tease, not what they give away."<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Walt Disney Studios and Lucasfilm presented a look at <i>The Force Awakens</i> at Disney's <a href="/wiki/Disney_D23" title="Disney D23" class="mw-redirect">D23 Expo</a> in August 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">[243]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Drew_Struzan" title="Drew Struzan">Drew Struzan</a>—who designed the poster artwork for the previous <i>Star Wars</i> films—produced a commemorative poster given to the event's attendees.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup> In October 2015, Lucasfilm unveiled the theatrical release poster and a third trailer.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">[245]</a></sup> The poster omitted Luke Skywalker and revealed a <a href="/wiki/Death_Star" title="Death Star">Death Star</a>-like "orb."<sup id="cite_ref-verge10202015_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-verge10202015-246">[246]</a></sup> The trailer debuted during the halftime break of <i><a href="/wiki/Monday_Night_Football" title="Monday Night Football">Monday Night Football</a></i>, before being released online.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">[247]</a></sup> The reaction to the trailer by fans on social media was "frenzied", with Lizo Mzimba of the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> writing that "perhaps the most significant thing about the final trailer before the film's release is how little of the story it reveals."<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">[248]</a></sup> Robbie Collin of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i> felt the trailer was "a perfect blend of old and new, in keeping with the old-fashioned <i>Star Wars</i> aesthetic."<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">[249]</a></sup> The trailer received 128 million views in 24 hours, a new record for the most views of a trailer in 24 hours. 16 million of the views came from its airing on <i>Monday Night Football</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">[250]</a></sup> At the end of October, <a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">Air France</a> announced a "Flight and Cinema" package, providing customers who book select flights to Paris transportation to a theater to see the film, since France is one of the first countries to release the film.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">[251]</a></sup> On November 6, a Japanese trailer for the film was released.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">[252]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">[253]</a></sup> After seeing the new trailer <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a>'</i> Ollie Barder stated the trailer gave him "hope" that the film would not "let us all down like the prequels did... [with] a worthwhile story this time."<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">[254]</a></sup> On November 23, a partnership with <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> was announced, in which Google users could choose to affiliate themselves with either the Dark or Light Side, which would change the appearance of their Google websites. Additionally, Disney teamed up with <a href="/wiki/Verizon_Wireless" title="Verizon Wireless">Verizon</a> to create a virtual-reality experience for <a href="/wiki/Google_Cardboard" title="Google Cardboard">Google Cardboard</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">[255]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>On December 17, 2015, select theaters across North America aired a <i>Star Wars</i> marathon, airing the six previous <i>Star Wars</i> episode films in 2D, followed by <i>The Force Awakens</i> in 3D. Attendees received a special lanyard featuring exclusive marathon art.<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">[256]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tie-in_literature_and_merchandise">Tie-in literature and merchandise</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Tie-in literature and merchandise">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Disney_Publishing_Worldwide" title="Disney Publishing Worldwide">Disney Publishing Worldwide</a> and Lucasfilm announced a series of "at least" 20 books and comics, titled "<a href="/wiki/Journey_to_Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens" title="Journey to Star Wars: The Force Awakens">Journey to <i>Star Wars: The Force Awakens</i></a>", with releases from multiple publishers starting in late 2015, prior to the film's premiere. The series includes books by Del Rey and Disney-Lucasfilm publishers and comic books from <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Comics" title="Marvel Comics">Marvel Comics</a>. All titles under the program are canonical to the <i>Star Wars</i> universe.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">[257]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">[258]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">[259]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alan_Dean_Foster" title="Alan Dean Foster">Alan Dean Foster</a> wrote a <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens_(novel)" title="Star Wars: The Force Awakens (novel)">novelization</a> of <i>The Force Awakens</i> which was released in e-book form on December 18.<sup id="cite_ref-jtrac_260-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jtrac-260">[260]</a></sup> In an effort to avoid revealing plot details before the film's release, the print release of the novelization was delayed until January 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-jtrac_260-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jtrac-260">[260]</a></sup> Marvel Comics will publish a five-issue comic book adaptation of <i>The Force Awakens</i> beginning in June 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">[261]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Disney_Consumer_Products" title="Disney Consumer Products">Disney Consumer Products</a> and Lucasfilm announced that September 4, 2015 would be deemed "Force Friday" and would be the official launch of all the merchandise for <i>The Force Awakens</i>. Beginning at 12:01 am, fans could buy toys, books, clothing and various other products at <a href="/wiki/Disney_Store" title="Disney Store">Disney Stores</a> and other retailers throughout the world.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">[262]</a></sup> Disney and <a href="/wiki/Maker_Studios" title="Maker Studios">Maker Studios</a> hosted an 18-hour <a href="/wiki/Streaming_media" title="Streaming media">live-streaming</a> presentation on YouTube, showcasing multiple merchandise products beginning on September 3, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">[263]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">[264]</a></sup> Among these products were a remote-controlled BB-8 developed by <a href="/wiki/Sphero" title="Sphero">Sphero</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Fortune_BB-8_174-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fortune_BB-8-174">[174]</a></sup> Sphero had participated in a Disney-run startup accelerator in July 2014, where they were invited into a private meeting with Disney CEO Bob Iger, in which they were shown on-set photos and imagery of BB-8 before its public unveiling.<sup id="cite_ref-wired-bb8_265-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wired-bb8-265">[265]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-thenational-bb8_266-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thenational-bb8-266">[266]</a></sup> Many retailers were unable to meet demand for <i>Star Wars</i> products.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">[267]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_media">Home media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Home media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_Home_Entertainment" title="Walt Disney Studios Home Entertainment">Walt Disney Studios Home Entertainment</a> released <i>Star Wars: The Force Awakens</i> via <a href="/wiki/Digital_distribution" title="Digital distribution">download</a> and <a href="/wiki/Disney_Movies_Anywhere" title="Disney Movies Anywhere">Disney Movies Anywhere</a> on April 1, 2016, with a <a href="/wiki/Blu-ray" title="Blu-ray">Blu-ray</a> and <a href="/wiki/DVD" title="DVD">DVD</a> released on April 5.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">[268]</a></sup> The home media release contains additional footage.<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">[269]</a></sup> On March 23, 2016, the film was <a href="/wiki/Copyright_infringement" title="Copyright infringement">leaked</a> online prior to its original Blu-ray release and was downloaded more than two million times in twelve hours.<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">[270]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>In January 2016, it was confirmed that <a href="/wiki/Starz" title="Starz">Starz</a> would hold the U.S. premium television rights for <i>The Force Awakens</i>, having been released just before the end of Starz's output deal covering most Disney-released films, which includes releases through the end of 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">[271]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">[272]</a></sup> The equivalent rights in Canada will be held by <a href="/wiki/Netflix" title="Netflix">Netflix</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">[273]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Box_office">Box office</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Box office">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_box_office_records_set_by_Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens" title="List of box office records set by Star Wars: The Force Awakens">List of box office records set by Star Wars: The Force Awakens</a>
     </div> 
     <p>As of April 13, 2016<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, <i>Star Wars: The Force Awakens</i> has grossed $935.6 million in North America and $1.129 billion in other territories for a worldwide total of $2.064 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-BOM_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-2">[2]</a></sup> <i>The Force Awakens</i> earned 8.6% of the total 2015 releases in North America, which is second only to the 8.8% of 1997 box office earned by <i><a href="/wiki/Titanic_(1997_film)" title="Titanic (1997 film)">Titanic</a></i> in 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">[274]</a></sup> The film is the <a href="/wiki/2015_in_film#Highest-grossing_films" title="2015 in film">highest-grossing release of 2015</a>, the highest-grossing film in the franchise (surpassing <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_Episode_I:_The_Phantom_Menace" title="Star Wars Episode I: The Phantom Menace" class="mw-redirect">The Phantom Menace</a></i>), the highest-grossing film released by <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_(division)" title="Walt Disney Studios (division)">Walt Disney Studios</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">[275]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films_in_Canada_and_the_United_States" title="List of highest-grossing films in Canada and the United States">highest-ever grossing film in North America</a> (dethroning <i><a href="/wiki/Avatar_(2009_film)" title="Avatar (2009 film)">Avatar</a></i>), and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest_grossing_films" title="List of highest grossing films" class="mw-redirect">third-highest-grossing film of all time</a>. It was the 24th film in cinematic history to surpass $1 billion worldwide, standing as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_fastest-grossing_films" title="List of fastest-grossing films">fastest film</a> to surpass the mark, doing so in 12 days.<sup id="cite_ref-fastest-to-1b1_276-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fastest-to-1b1-276">[276]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fastest-to-1b2_277-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fastest-to-1b2-277">[277]</a></sup> It was the third film in history to surpass $2 billion worldwide, doing so on its 53rd day of release.<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">[278]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Deadline.com" title="Deadline.com">Deadline.com</a> calculated the net profit of the film to be $923.8 million, when factoring together all expenses and revenues for the film, making it the most profitable film of 2015 and the most profitable film in the last seven years.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">[279]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">[280]</a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Theatrical_run">Theatrical run</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Theatrical run">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
     <p><i>The Force Awakens</i> was released in the United States and Canada on December 18, 2015. It made a record-breaking $57 million from Thursday night previews,<sup id="cite_ref-Star_Wars:The_Force_Awaken_theatrical_run_284-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Star_Wars:The_Force_Awaken_theatrical_run-284">[N 1]</a></sup> of which IMAX screenings generated a record-breaking $5.7 million from 391 screens.<sup id="cite_ref-force3_285-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-force3-285">[284]</a></sup> On its opening day, the film grossed $119.1 million from 14,300 screens, marking the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_openings_for_films#Biggest_opening_day_in_U.S._and_Canada" title="List of highest-grossing openings for films">biggest single and opening day</a> record<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">[285]</a></sup> and the first time a film has earned more than $100 million in a single day.<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">[286]</a></sup> Without Thursday night grosses, the film earned the second largest opening-day gross ($62.1 million).<sup id="cite_ref-SM_288-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SM-288">[287]</a></sup> In total, it earned a record $247,966,675 for its debut weekend from nearly 28.8 million tickets sold,<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">[288]</a></sup> including an IMAX opening-weekend record of $30.1 million (12.65%) from 391 IMAX theaters,<sup id="cite_ref-USopen_290-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USopen-290">[289]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IMAXdead_291-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMAXdead-291">[290]</a></sup> which nearly amounts to the $252.5 million total earned by <i><a href="/wiki/Return_of_the_Jedi" title="Return of the Jedi">Return of the Jedi</a></i> – the 2nd lowest-grossing film in the series – in its original run.<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">[291]</a></sup> Minus the $57 million it earned from previews, the film earned $190.8 million on straight Friday to Sunday, giving it an average of $63.6 million per day.<sup id="cite_ref-SM_288-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SM-288">[287]</a></sup> 2D screenings accounted for 53% of the total opening gross while 3D accounted for 47%. <a href="/wiki/RealD_3D" title="RealD 3D">RealD 3D</a> comprised $78 million of the opening gross, setting a new record.<sup id="cite_ref-USopen_290-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USopen-290">[289]</a></sup> Other records set by the film include the biggest weekend per-theater average for a wide release ($59,982 per theater),<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">[292]</a></sup> biggest holiday opening,<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">[293]</a></sup> biggest PG-13 rated opening,<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">[294]</a></sup> and biggest December opening.<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">[295]</a></sup> The opening-weekend audience was evenly split among those under and over the age of 25, with 58% of the audience male, 71% adults, 20% families and 9% teenagers.<sup id="cite_ref-SM_288-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SM-288">[287]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Internationally, the film was released in over 30,000 screens.<sup id="cite_ref-Intldead_297-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Intldead-297">[296]</a></sup> It opened on December 16, 2015 in 12 international markets and earned $14.1 million on its opening day, debuting at first place in all of them.<sup id="cite_ref-force_298-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-force-298">[297]</a></sup> It expanded in an additional 42 countries on December 17, generating $58.6 million for a two-day international total of $72.7 million, reaching first place in all 44 markets.<sup id="cite_ref-deadline_299-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deadline-299">[298]</a></sup> It grossed a total of $129.5 million in three days after adding $56.8 million on its third day, topped the daily box office in all countries except for South Korea where it was the second,<sup id="cite_ref-deadline_299-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deadline-299">[298]</a></sup> and set a new midnight record in the United Kingdom with $3.6 million.<sup id="cite_ref-force2_300-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-force2-300">[299]</a></sup> It broke opening day records in the UK, Ireland and Malta ($14.3 million), Germany ($7.1 million), Australia ($6.8 million), Sweden ($1.7 million), Norway ($1.1 million) and in 16 other countries.<sup id="cite_ref-force3_285-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-force3-285">[284]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-force_298-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-force-298">[297]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-force2_300-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-force2-300">[299]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">[300]</a></sup> Other markets which generated large opening days were Spain ($3.5 million), Mexico ($3.4 million), Italy ($3.1 million) and Japan ($3 million).<sup id="cite_ref-deadline_299-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deadline-299">[298]</a></sup> After the five days, <i>The Force Awakens</i> had a total international opening gross of $281 million from 30,000 screens in 72 markets, a new record for December opening<sup id="cite_ref-Intldead_297-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Intldead-297">[296]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TGIF_302-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TGIF-302">[301]</a></sup> and the third biggest international opening of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">[302]</a></sup> International markets generating opening weekend tallies of at least $10 million were the United Kingdom, Ireland and Malta ($50.6 million), Germany ($27.5 million), France ($22.5 million), Australia ($19.6 million) and Japan ($13.4 million) and Russia ($12.3 million). The film had the biggest opening of all time in 18 countries including the United Kingdom, Germany, Australia, Russia and Sweden.<sup id="cite_ref-Intldead_297-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Intldead-297">[296]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Overseas21stOpening_304-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas21stOpening-304">[303]</a></sup> IMAX generated $17.9 million from 276 IMAX theaters.<sup id="cite_ref-IMAXdead_291-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMAXdead-291">[290]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>After five days, the film had a total worldwide opening record of $529 million from 74 territories, which is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_openings_for_films#Biggest_worldwide_openings_since_2002" title="List of highest-grossing openings for films">biggest worldwide opening</a>, making it only the second time in cinematic history – after <i><a href="/wiki/Jurassic_World" title="Jurassic World">Jurassic World</a></i> – that a film had opened to more than $500 million globally.<sup id="cite_ref-TGIF_302-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TGIF-302">[301]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ttt_305-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ttt-305">[304]</a></sup> This included an IMAX opening record of $48 million.<sup id="cite_ref-Ttt_305-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ttt-305">[304]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Revenues in the film's <a href="/wiki/Second_weekend_in_box_office_performance" title="Second weekend in box office performance">second weekend</a> decreased by only 39.8% in the United States and Canada, earning $149.2 million, to remain in first place at the box office<sup id="cite_ref-BOM2_306-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOM2-306">[305]</a></sup> and recording the biggest second weekend of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">[306]</a></sup> Revenues from IMAX also dipped slightly, generating $19 million in its second weekend, for a record total of over $70 million in 10 days.<sup id="cite_ref-Deadline2_308-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Deadline2-308">[307]</a></sup> Internationally, the film had a steeper decline in its second weekend, falling 51% to $136.9 million.<sup id="cite_ref-SW2_309-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SW2-309">[308]</a></sup> Of the notable major markets, the film had an unsuccessful opening in India where it opened third against two local blockbusters with a mere $1.51 million.<sup id="cite_ref-310" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-310">[309]</a></sup> As of February 21, the largest markets outside of the United States and Canada are the United Kingdom ($180.7 million), China ($124.5 million), Germany ($109.7 million), Japan ($92.6 million) and France ($88.2 million).<sup id="cite_ref-Overseas8thOpening_311-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas8thOpening-311">[310]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><i>The Force Awakens</i> crossed the $1 billion mark on the 12th day of its general release (December 26, 2015), making it the fastest film to reach this mark. It became the twenty-fourth film grossing more than $1 billion worldwide, and the <a href="/wiki/2015_in_film" title="2015 in film">fifth film of 2015</a> to do so, making 2015 the first year to have five films gross more than $1 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-Deadline2_308-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Deadline2-308">[307]</a></sup> The film experienced another decrease in revenue in its third weekend, dropping 40.8% to $88.2 domestically, remaining in first place at the box office,<sup id="cite_ref-312" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-312">[311]</a></sup> to set a third-weekend record.<sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313">[312]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>On January 2, after just 16 days of release, it became the second film (following <i>Avatar</i>) to gross over $700 million in North America,<sup id="cite_ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314">[313]</a></sup> and on January 6 became the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films_in_Canada_and_the_United_States" title="List of highest-grossing films in Canada and the United States">highest-grossing film of all time domestically</a>, doing so in 20 days.<sup id="cite_ref-315" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-315">[314]</a></sup> On January 9, it became the first film in cinematic history to cross $800 million domestically unadjusted for inflation,<sup id="cite_ref-IMAXfast_316-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMAXfast-316">[315]</a></sup> and in the same weekend set a Saturday to Sunday opening weekend record for the studio in China with $52.6 million.<sup id="cite_ref-Overseas2ndOpening_317-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas2ndOpening-317">[316]</a></sup> On January 17, 2016, it passed the $1 billion mark overseas becoming the first film of Disney, the third film of 2015 and the fifth film overall to achieve this feat.<sup id="cite_ref-Overseas3rdOpening_318-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas3rdOpening-318">[317]</a></sup> It topped the international box office chart for five consecutive weekends, becoming the first film since <i><a href="/wiki/Avengers:_Age_of_Ultron" title="Avengers: Age of Ultron">Avengers: Age of Ultron</a></i> to have five straight wins, before being dethroned by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Revenant_(2015_film)" title="The Revenant (2015 film)">The Revenant</a></i> in its sixth weekend.<sup id="cite_ref-Overseas4thOpening_319-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas4thOpening-319">[318]</a></sup> In Japan, it topped the box office for six straight weekends.<sup id="cite_ref-Overseas4thOpening_319-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas4thOpening-319">[318]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>On February 5, <i>The Force Awakens</i> became the first film to earn over $900 million in the United States and Canada, doing so on its fiftieth day of release, becoming the first film to reach that milestone unadjusted for inflation.<sup id="cite_ref-320" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-320">[319]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-321" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-321">[320]</a></sup> On the following day, it became the third film in cinematic history to pass $2 billion in ticket sales worldwide (after <i><a href="/wiki/Titanic_(1997_film)" title="Titanic (1997 film)">Titanic</a></i> and <i>Avatar</i>) and the second in original release (after <i>Avatar</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-Overseas6thOpening_322-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas6thOpening-322">[321]</a></sup> Also, it became the third film to earn over $600 million in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-Overseas6thOpening_322-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas6thOpening-322">[321]</a></sup> In North America and the United Kingdom and Ireland, it fell outside of the top ten for the first time in its eleventh weekend respectively during the weekend February 26–28, 2016,<sup id="cite_ref-323" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-323">[322]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-324" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-324">[323]</a></sup> and in the U.S. it fell off $1 million for the first time in its fourteenth weekend.<sup id="cite_ref-325" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-325">[324]</a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_analysis">Commercial analysis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Commercial analysis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
     <p>With a production budget of $200 million,<sup id="cite_ref-Deadline_profit_326-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Deadline_profit-326">[325]</a></sup> plus $175 million for marketing, printing and advertising costs, <i>The Force Awakens</i> was predicted to be a major box office success.<sup id="cite_ref-327" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-327">[326]</a></sup> The cost of the film was subsidized by £31.6 million ($47 million USD) from the UK film incentive program.<sup id="cite_ref-politico.eu_328-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-politico.eu-328">[327]</a></sup> Total costs, after accounting for profit participations, production and distribution of home videos, as well as other ancillary mediums, is expected to run $423 million. <sup id="cite_ref-329" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-329">[328]</a></sup> Reports in April 2015 from <i>The Hollywood Reporter</i> and Amboee Brand Intelligence predicted the film would earn up to $540 million worldwide for its opening, breaking the record for the biggest worldwide opening, as well as breaking the record for the biggest U.S. opening. They also believed that <i>The Force Awakens</i> would have the widest release ever, across 4,500 theaters in North America.<sup id="cite_ref-BOX_330-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOX-330">[329]</a></sup> But it ended receiving a total of 4,134 theaters, and nevertheless had the widest December opening.<sup id="cite_ref-theforce1_204-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theforce1-204">[204]</a></sup> Box office analyst, Phil Contrino likened the film to <i>Avatar</i> (2009), which opened to $77 million in North America and went on to earn $2.8 billion worldwide, saying <i>The Force Awakens</i> would earn $1 billion "without blinking" and could cross $2 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-BOX_330-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOX-330">[329]</a></sup> In August 2015, <a href="/wiki/Deadline.com" title="Deadline.com">Deadline.com</a> predicted an opening weekend of $615 million worldwide could be possible, including a $300 million opening in North America.<sup id="cite_ref-DEAD_2_331-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DEAD_2-331">[330]</a></sup> In November, box office analysts reported opening weekend projections were at $175–250 million.<sup id="cite_ref-theforce1_204-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theforce1-204">[204]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DEAD_3_332-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DEAD_3-332">[331]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-333" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-333">[332]</a></sup> In December, capital analyst Barton Crockett suggested that the film will be the first to gross over $3 billion worldwide at the box office.<sup id="cite_ref-.27Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens.27_Tracking_Suggests_Film_Could_Make_.242.7_Billion_Profit_334-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-.27Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens.27_Tracking_Suggests_Film_Could_Make_.242.7_Billion_Profit-334">[333]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Analysts said that the box office receipts of the film, when compared to predecessors, must be adjusted for inflation, and that the first <i>Star Wars</i> film made more when this adjustment is made.<sup id="cite_ref-Stock_335-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stock-335">[334]</a></sup> It has further been observed that each of the first three films in the series was more profitable in calculating revenue against production costs.<sup id="cite_ref-Stock_335-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stock-335">[334]</a></sup> Paul Dergarabedian, one of Hollywood's best-known box office analysts, said that while <i>Avatar</i> and <i>The Force Awakens</i> were both released on the same date of December 18, higher ticket prices in 2015 and IMAX screenings could push <i>Star Wars</i> "into the box office stratosphere".<sup id="cite_ref-336" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-336">[335]</a></sup> On December 23, Mark Hughes of <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> stated that <i>The Force Awakens</i> had matched the most optimistic projections for its opening, and he predicted that <i>The Force Awakens</i> would likely surpass <i>Titanic</i> as the second-highest-grossing film of all time. He also stated that <i>The Force Awakens</i> could catch <i>Avatar</i> as the top-grossing film of all time, but only if it managed to avoid major week-to-week declines in ticket sales.<sup id="cite_ref-mhughes_337-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mhughes-337">[336]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>By January 13, analysts concluded that it was unlikely that <i>The Force Awakens</i> would surpass <i>Avatar'</i>s global gross.<sup id="cite_ref-McClintock_338-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McClintock-338">[337]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Eggertse_339-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eggertse-339">[338]</a></sup> While <i>The Force Awakens</i> is hugely successful in North America, the same success was not witnessed in many overseas individual markets such as Germany, India, Latin America and parts of Asia. Cited reasons for this is that overseas audiences do not have the same nostalgia or affinity for the film as those in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-McClintock_338-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McClintock-338">[337]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Eggertse_339-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eggertse-339">[338]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Tartaglione_340-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tartaglione-340">[339]</a></sup> The <i>Star Wars</i> franchise has also traditionally lacked resonance with filmgoers in China, which is why part of the marketing for <i>The Force Awakens</i> heavily focused on appealing to that territory.<sup id="cite_ref-Eggertse_339-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eggertse-339">[338]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Tartaglione2_341-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tartaglione2-341">[340]</a></sup> Pamela McClintock stated that, for these territories, <i>Star Wars</i> "doesn't have the same legacy as it does in North America and more mature markets. It's also a faster burn, meaning it likely won't stay in theaters as long as <i>Avatar</i> did."<sup id="cite_ref-McClintock_338-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McClintock-338">[337]</a></sup> Dergarabedian said, "As in all box-office trajectories, the higher the altitude, the tougher it becomes to rack up sales at the kind of breakneck pace as in the beginning of the run."<sup id="cite_ref-McClintock_338-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McClintock-338">[337]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Nancy Tartaglione of Deadline.com argued that, if accounting for its 40/60 domestic to international split, <i>The Force Awakens</i> did well overseas.<sup id="cite_ref-Tartaglione_340-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tartaglione-340">[339]</a></sup> <i>Avatar</i> did well internationally because of its novelty, the marketing campaign advertising it as showcasing the newest 3D technology that can only be fully appreciated in the theaters, and because of its extended time in overseas theaters.<sup id="cite_ref-Eggertse_339-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eggertse-339">[338]</a></sup> While <i>The Force Awakens</i> had appeal with its special effects, analysts feel that it lacked the novelty factor; they also cite that its gross was additionally stilted due to markets making way for new films sooner than was previously done. Films do not play in overseas theaters as long as they did back when <i>Avatar</i> was released.<sup id="cite_ref-Eggertse_339-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eggertse-339">[338]</a></sup> Dergarabedian stated, "No matter what, [<i>The Force Awakens</i>] is an absolute, all-out blockbuster without peer in terms of the sheer speed at which it has crossed all of these major box-office milestones."<sup id="cite_ref-McClintock_338-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McClintock-338">[337]</a></sup> Moreover, Mike Fleming of Deadline.com argued that the movie was the "most valuable movie" of the year, with "the net profit to Disney an astounding $923M, and the Cash on Cash Return twice that of any other film [released in 2016], at 2.31".<sup id="cite_ref-Deadline_profit_326-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Deadline_profit-326">[325]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_response">Critical response</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Critical response">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p><i>Star Wars: The Force Awakens</i> received mostly positive reviews from critics.<sup id="cite_ref-342" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-342">[341]</a></sup> On <a href="/wiki/Review_aggregator" title="Review aggregator">review aggregator</a> website <a href="/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes" title="Rotten Tomatoes">Rotten Tomatoes</a>, it has a 92% approval rating, based on 342 reviews, with a <a href="/wiki/Rating_average" title="Rating average" class="mw-redirect">rating average</a> of 8.2/10. The website's critical consensus reads, "Packed with action and populated by both familiar faces and fresh blood, <i>The Force Awakens</i> successfully recalls the series' former glory while injecting it with renewed energy."<sup id="cite_ref-343" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-343">[342]</a></sup> On <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>, the film has a score of 81 out of 100, based on 52 critics, indicating "universal acclaim".<sup id="cite_ref-344" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-344">[343]</a></sup> On <a href="/wiki/CinemaScore" title="CinemaScore">CinemaScore</a>, audiences gave the film an average grade of "A" on an A+ to F scale; women, under-25s and under-18s gave it an "A+", while 98% of audiences gave it an "A" or "B".<sup id="cite_ref-CinemaScore_345-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CinemaScore-345">[344]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Robbie_Collin" title="Robbie Collin">Robbie Collin</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i> gave <i>The Force Awakens</i> five stars out of five and wrote that it "sets out to shake <i>Star Wars</i> from its slumber, and reconnect the series with its much-pined-for past. That it achieves this both immediately and joyously is perhaps the single greatest relief of the movie-going year."<sup id="cite_ref-346" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-346">[345]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Peter_Bradshaw" title="Peter Bradshaw">Peter Bradshaw</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> gave it five stars out of five, writing that it was "both a narrative progression from the earlier three films and a shrewdly affectionate next-gen reboot&nbsp;... ridiculous and melodramatic and sentimental of course, but exciting and brimming with energy and its own kind of generosity."<sup id="cite_ref-347" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-347">[346]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s Justin Chang wrote that the film has "sufficient style, momentum, love and care to prove irresistible to any who have ever considered themselves fans."<sup id="cite_ref-Justin_Chang_348-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Justin_Chang-348">[347]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Richard_Roeper" title="Richard Roeper">Richard Roeper</a> of the <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Sun-Times" title="Chicago Sun-Times">Chicago Sun-Times</a></i> gave the film four stars out of four, describing it as "a beautiful, thrilling, joyous, surprising and heart-thumping adventure."<sup id="cite_ref-Chicago_Sun-TimesR_349-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chicago_Sun-TimesR-349">[348]</a></sup> Tom Long of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Detroit_News" title="The Detroit News">The Detroit News</a></i> wrote that though some may find the film too similar to the original <i>Star Wars</i>, it leaves "the ungainly and unneeded clumsiness of the subsequent prequels far behind&nbsp;... the energy, humor and simplicity of direction [has] been recaptured."<sup id="cite_ref-350" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-350">[349]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a> called it "basically the same" as the original film, but "isn't that what we all wanted anyway?"<sup id="cite_ref-351" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-351">[350]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Ann Hornaday, writing for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i>, thought the film had "enough novelty to create yet another cohort of die-hard fans&nbsp;... <i>The Force Awakens</i> strikes all the right chords, emotional and narrative, to feel both familiar and exhilaratingly new."<sup id="cite_ref-W._Post:_Hornaday_352-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-W._Post:_Hornaday-352">[351]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Orr_(film_critic)" title="Christopher Orr (film critic)">Christopher Orr</a>, writing in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Atlantic" title="The Atlantic">The Atlantic</a></i>, called the film "a mashup masterpiece" that "may be completely derivative" but is "a delight nonetheless."<sup id="cite_ref-353" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-353">[352]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Charlotte_Observer" title="The Charlotte Observer">The Charlotte Observer</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s Lawrence Toppman said Abrams had "pulled off a delicate balancing act, paying clever homage to the past."<sup id="cite_ref-354" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-354">[353]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mick_LaSalle" title="Mick LaSalle">Mick LaSalle</a> of the <i><a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Chronicle" title="San Francisco Chronicle">San Francisco Chronicle</a></i> gave the film his highest rating and called it "the best <i>Star Wars</i> sequel yet and one of the best films of 2015."<sup id="cite_ref-355" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-355">[354]</a></sup> Frank Pallotta, reviewing the film for <a href="/wiki/CNNMoney" title="CNNMoney">CNN Money</a>, found it was the best <i>Star Wars</i> film since the original trilogy and that it "is bound to be a film experience long remembered by fans and non-fans alike."<sup id="cite_ref-CNNreview_356-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNNreview-356">[355]</a></sup> Jack Bottomley, writing for <i><a href="/wiki/Starburst_(magazine)" title="Starburst (magazine)">Starburst</a></i>, awarded the film 10 out of 10 saying, "From old joys to fresh twists, this is a unique blockbuster experience that celebrates the franchise whilst also expanding it."<sup id="cite_ref-357" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-357">[356]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Some critics found the film too derivative of previous <i>Star Wars</i> films.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT-20151231_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20151231-88">[88]</a></sup> Andrew O'Hehir wrote for <a href="/wiki/Salon_(website)" title="Salon (website)"><i>Salon</i></a> that it was "the work of a talented mimic or ventriloquist who can just about cover for the fact that he has nothing much to say."<sup id="cite_ref-358" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-358">[357]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stephanie_Zacharek" title="Stephanie Zacharek">Stephanie Zacharek</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> wrote that Abrams had delivered "everything we expect, as opposed to those nebulous wonders we didn't know we wanted."<sup id="cite_ref-359" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-359">[358]</a></sup> Reviewing for <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i>, Scott Mendelson cited the film's "top-tier production values and a strong sense of scale and scope", but felt it was so much "an exercise in fan service [that] it is only due to the charisma and talent of our newbies and J. J. Abrams' undeniable skill as a visual storyteller that the <a href="/wiki/Mad_Libs" title="Mad Libs">Mad Libs</a> narrative doesn't outright destroy the picture."<sup id="cite_ref-360" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-360">[359]</a></sup> Brian Merchant wrote for <i>Motherboard</i>: "Science fiction is supposed to be all about exploring the unexplored, not rehashing the well-trod ... one of the most unabashedly creative enterprises of the 20th century has been rendered another largely enjoyable, but mostly forgettable Hollywood reboot."<sup id="cite_ref-361" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-361">[360]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Accolades">Accolades</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Accolades">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_accolades_received_by_Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens" title="List of accolades received by Star Wars: The Force Awakens">List of accolades received by Star Wars: The Force Awakens</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Several awards held their nominations before the December release of <i>The Force Awakens</i>, making the film ineligible for the <a href="/wiki/73rd_Golden_Globe_Awards" title="73rd Golden Globe Awards">73rd Golden Globe Awards</a> and some other awards ceremonies.<sup id="cite_ref-lateawards_362-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lateawards-362">[361]</a></sup> However, the film was added to the <a href="/wiki/21st_Critics%27_Choice_Awards" title="21st Critics' Choice Awards">21st Critics' Choice Awards</a>'s slate of best picture nominees after a special vote by the board of directors,<sup id="cite_ref-cca15_363-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cca15-363">[362]</a></sup> and the announcement of the <a href="/wiki/American_Film_Institute_Awards_2015" title="American Film Institute Awards 2015">2015 American Film Institute Awards</a> was delayed until after the release of <i>The Force Awakens</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-lateawards_362-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lateawards-362">[361]</a></sup> The film received five <a href="/wiki/88th_Academy_Awards" title="88th Academy Awards">Academy Award</a> nominations and became the most <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Award" title="Saturn Award">Saturn Award</a>-nominated film in history, receiving fifteen nominations.</p>

     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Top_ten_lists">Top ten lists</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Top ten lists">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
     <p>In addition to several awards and nominations, <i>The Force Awakens</i> appeared on several critics' lists of the ten best films of 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-386" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-386">[385]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2;"> 
      <ul> 
       <li>1st&nbsp;– Peter Howell, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Toronto_Star" title="The Toronto Star" class="mw-redirect">The Toronto Star</a></i></li> 
       <li>2nd&nbsp;– Bob Thompson, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Vancouver_Sun" title="The Vancouver Sun">The Vancouver Sun</a></i></li> 
       <li>3rd&nbsp;– <i><a href="/wiki/Total_Film" title="Total Film">Total Film</a></i></li> 
       <li>4th&nbsp;– <i><a href="/wiki/Digital_Spy" title="Digital Spy">Digital Spy</a></i></li> 
       <li>4th&nbsp;– Rod Pocowatchit, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wichita_Eagle" title="The Wichita Eagle">The Wichita Eagle</a></i></li> 
       <li>4th&nbsp;– Troy L. Smith, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Plain_Dealer" title="The Plain Dealer">The Plain Dealer</a></i></li> 
       <li>5th&nbsp;– <i><a href="/wiki/Empire_(film_magazine)" title="Empire (film magazine)">Empire</a></i></li> 
       <li>5th&nbsp;– <i><a href="/wiki/Wired_(magazine)" title="Wired (magazine)">Wired</a></i></li> 
       <li>5th&nbsp;– Collin Souter, <a href="/wiki/Roger_Ebert" title="Roger Ebert">RogerEbert.com</a></li> 
       <li>6th&nbsp;- Michael Smith, <i><a href="/wiki/Tulsa_World" title="Tulsa World">Tulsa World</a></i></li> 
       <li>6th&nbsp;- <i><a href="/wiki/Twitch_Film" title="Twitch Film">Twitch Film</a></i></li> 
       <li>7th&nbsp;– <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Jacobs" title="Matthew Jacobs">Matthew Jacobs</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Huffington_Post" title="The Huffington Post">The Huffington Post</a></i></li> 
       <li>7th&nbsp;– Peter Debruge, <i><a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a></i></li> 
       <li>8th&nbsp;– Matt Fagerholm, <a href="/wiki/Roger_Ebert" title="Roger Ebert">RogerEbert.com</a></li> 
       <li>9th&nbsp;– Sean P. Means, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Salt_Lake_Tribune" title="The Salt Lake Tribune">The Salt Lake Tribune</a></i></li> 
       <li>9th&nbsp;– <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Orr_(film_critic)" title="Christopher Orr (film critic)">Christopher Orr</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Atlantic" title="The Atlantic">The Atlantic</a></i></li> 
       <li>9th&nbsp;– <a href="/wiki/Richard_Roeper" title="Richard Roeper">Richard Roeper</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Chicago_Sun-Times" title="The Chicago Sun-Times" class="mw-redirect">The Chicago Sun-Times</a></i></li> 
       <li>9th&nbsp;– <a href="/wiki/Peter_Travers" title="Peter Travers">Peter Travers</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i></li> 
       <li>10th&nbsp;– <a href="/wiki/Robbie_Collin" title="Robbie Collin">Robbie Collin</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i></li> 
       <li>10th&nbsp;– <a href="/wiki/Mick_LaSalle" title="Mick LaSalle">Mick LaSalle</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Chronicle" title="San Francisco Chronicle">San Francisco Chronicle</a></i></li> 
       <li>Top 10 (ordered alphabetically)&nbsp;– <a href="/wiki/American_Film_Institute" title="American Film Institute">American Film Institute</a></li> 
       <li>Top 10 (ordered alphabetically)&nbsp;– <a href="/wiki/Peter_Bradshaw" title="Peter Bradshaw">Peter Bradshaw</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i></li> 
       <li>Top 10 (ordered alphabetically)&nbsp;– <a href="/wiki/Joe_Leydon" title="Joe Leydon">Joe Leydon</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a></i></li> 
       <li>Top 10 (ordered alphabetically)&nbsp;– <a href="/wiki/Nell_Minow" title="Nell Minow">Nell Minow</a>, RogerEbert.com</li> 
       <li>Top 10 (ordered alphabetically)&nbsp;– <a href="/wiki/Joe_Morgenstern" title="Joe Morgenstern">Joe Morgenstern</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a></i></li>

      <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_VIII" title="Star Wars: Episode VIII">Star Wars: Episode VIII</a>
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Rian_Johnson" title="Rian Johnson">Rian Johnson</a> confirmed in August 2014 that he would direct <i>Episode VIII</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-THRJohnson_172-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-THRJohnson-172">[172]</a></sup> It is scheduled for release on December 15, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-387" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-387">[386]</a></sup> Some second-unit filming took place in September 2015 in Ireland,<sup id="cite_ref-388" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-388">[387]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-389" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-389">[388]</a></sup> with principal photography beginning in February 2016 at Pinewood Studios.<sup id="cite_ref-390" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-390">[389]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-391" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-391">[390]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-THR2_392-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-THR2-392">[391]</a></sup> Hamill, Fisher, Driver, Ridley, Boyega, Isaac, Nyong'o, Gleeson, Daniels, Christie, Serkis, and Mayhew reprise their roles in the film, and are joined by <a href="/wiki/Benicio_del_Toro" title="Benicio del Toro">Benicio del Toro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Laura_Dern" title="Laura Dern">Laura Dern</a> and Kelly Marie Tran.<sup id="cite_ref-393" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-393">[392]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Vee" title="Jimmy Vee">Jimmy Vee</a> will replace Baker as R2-D2.<sup id="cite_ref-394" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-394">[393]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-395" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-395">[394]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Episode_IX"><i>Episode IX</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Episode IX">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote">
      Further information: 
      <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_IX" title="Star Wars: Episode IX" class="mw-redirect">Star Wars: Episode IX</a>
     </div> 
     <p>In August 2015, <a href="/wiki/Colin_Trevorrow" title="Colin Trevorrow">Colin Trevorrow</a> was announced as the director of <i>Episode IX</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-396" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-396">[395]</a></sup> scheduled for release on May 24, 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-397" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-397">[396]</a></sup></p>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Footnote">Footnote</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Footnote">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;"> 
      <ol class="references"> 
       <li id="cite_note-Star_Wars:The_Force_Awaken_theatrical_run-284"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Star_Wars:The_Force_Awaken_theatrical_run_284-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The $57 million figure incorporates revenues generated from the "<i>Star Wars</i> Marathon Event" from 135 theaters in which all previous six <i>Star Wars</i> films were shown along with <i>Star Wars: The Force Awakens</i>. Ticket prices cost $59.99 for all the films (including <i>The Force Awakens</i>) at an average of $8.57 per movie.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">[281]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">[282]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">[283]</a></sup></span></li> 
      </ol> 
     </div>
